Her case was published in CTN News.</p>\n<p>With the dangerous COVID-19 mRNA shots now being extended to babies and toddlers, I decided to search the Government VAERS (Vaccine Adverse Reporting System) database for cases filed for various eye disorders.</p>\n<p>For the past 18 months since the COVID-19 vaccines were given emergency use authorizations, there have been 17,858 cases of eye disorders reported, including 59 deaths, 1,232 permanent disabilities, 2,882 ER visits, and 1,466 hospitalizations, with 307 life threatening events.</p>\n<p>That&#8217;s an average of 992 cases of eye disorders reported each month following COVID-19 vaccine injections, and this is most certainly NOT an exhaustive list of eye disorders.</p>\n<p>But it does give us a sub-set of data to compare to all other FDA-approved vaccines for the previous 30 years (360 months) prior to the roll out of the COVID-19 vaccines.</p>\n<p>Using this exact same set of eye disorders, we find 11,898 cases filed for eye disorders over the course of 30 years following all other FDA-approved vaccines, which averages out to 33 cases a month.</p>\n<p>So that is 2,902% increase in eye disorders following the very dangerous COVID-19 vaccines, which the health &#8220;authorities&#8221; medically and politically.</p>\n<p>It cuts to the heart of the hottest button question of all about the mRNA shots, whether they have hidden fertility risks. title="https://healthimpactnews.com/2022/fifth-largest-life-insurance-company-in-us-paid-out-163-more-for-deaths-of-working-people-ages-18-64-in-2021-after-covid-19-vaccine-mandates/">Fifth Largest Life Insurance Company in US Paid Out 163% More for Deaths of Working People ages 18-64 in 2021 After COVID-19 Vaccine Mandates</a></h2><p>Five months after breaking the story of the CEO of One America insurance company saying deaths among working people ages 18-64 were up 40% in the third quarter of 2021, I can report that a much larger life insurance company, Lincoln National, reported a 163% increase in death benefits paid out under its group life insurance policies in 2021.</p>\n<p>This is according to the annual statements filed with state insurance departments \xe2\x80\x94 statements that were provided exclusively to Crossroads Report in response to public records requests.</p>\n<p>The reports show a more extreme situation than the 40% increase in deaths in the third quarter of 2021 that was cited in late December by One America CEO Scott Davison \xe2\x80\x94 an increase that he said was industry-wide and that he described at the time as \xe2\x80\x9cunheard of\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9chuge, huge numbers\xe2\x80\x9d and the highest death rates that have\xc2\xa0ever been seen in the history of the life insurance business.</p>\n<p>The annual statements for Lincoln National Life Insurance Company show that the company paid out in death benefits under group life insurance policies a little over\xc2\xa0$500 million\xc2\xa0in 2019, about\xc2\xa0$548 million in 2020, and a stunning\xc2\xa0$1.4 billion\xc2\xa0in 2021.</p>\n<p>From 2019, the last normal year before the pandemic, to 2020, the year of the Covid-19 virus, there was an increase in group death benefits paid out of only\xc2\xa09 percent. Prior to the industrial age post WWII, most neighborhoods had local businesses and farmers who supplied the bulk of that community&#8217;s food, from the milkman who delivered dairy products, to the town butcher who processed meat, to the town baker who produced products from grains, etc.</p>\n<p>There was no one-stop shop where one could pick up multiple products called &#8220;groceries.&#8221; Few understand that the modern day grocery store is dependent on a highly technical system that is interdependent on many inputs into the supply chain, and can easily be ground to a halt.</p>\n<p>If you have lived through local natural disasters, like a hurricane, or an earthquake, you probably have had a taste of what it can be like when everyone all of sudden needs to buy groceries all at the same time, and then learn that the grocery store shelves are bare.</p>\n<p>Panic buying can cause similar disruptions, and most of us got a taste, and that&#8217;s all it was, a &#8220;taste&#8221;, of this in the early days of the COVID-19 lockdowns.</p>\n<p>But almost all of the people alive in the U.S. today have not experienced real hardship that produces hunger and starvation, such as what this nation experienced in the 1930s prior to WWII during the &#8220;dust bowl&#8221; as the nation suffered an economic depression, along with massive food shortages due to crop failures.</p>\n<p>We have had economic downturns since WWII, but in general the U.S. has seen prosperous times for over 70 years now, and the current generations alive have become so dependent on the conveniences that modern technology has brought us, that they just assume it will always be there, and fail to realize just how fragile that technology is.</p>\n<p>Today, less than 1% of the population of the United States now produces food for the other 99%, thanks to the technological age, so when farmers, particularly farmers with contracts in the commodity food industry, which is by far the majority, speak out with warnings about what is ahead, it is time to sit up and listen, and realize that if you cannot buy food from your usual local grocery outlets, that there will be no one to bail you out if you have not prepared for such a situation.</p>\n<p>For the rest of this article I am publishing some news today that farmers themselves are reporting, and everyone needs to take heed and prepare accordingly.</p>\n</div><div class="fusion-clearfix"></div></div>\r\n\t\t\t\t</div></div>\r\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\r\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\r\n\t\t\t\t<div class="fusion-blog-shortcode fusion-blog-medium fusion-blog-infinite"><div class="fusion-posts-container posts-container-infinite">\r\n\t\t\t\t<div class="post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail">\r\n\t\t\t\t<div class="blog-medium-slideshow-container"><div class="fusion-flexslider flexslider blog-medium-image floated-post-slideshow" style="height: 119px;">\r\n\t\t\t\t<ul class="slides"><li class="flex-active-slide" style="width: 100%; Take\xc2\xa0this article\xc2\xa0about Union Pacific, for example. UP has been removing up to 3% of railroad-controlled cars from the network, in order to manage the current congestion. The number of cars on the UP system, however, remains on the rise.</p>\n<p>How can we conceptualize this? </p>\n<p>Just how bad is this new &#8220;outbreak&#8221; which now threatens the world in a similar way to how COVID threatened to wipe out humanity?</p>\n<p>Cases of monkeypox in the UK doubled this week &#8211; to an &#8220;alarming&#8221; 20 cases. And it is now spreading to the U.S. at an alarming rate, as one person has reportedly now tested positive for it (determined by the PCR test apparently) in New York City. </p>\n<p>It appears that worldwide this &#8220;alarming spread&#8221; of monkeypox is well below 100 cases at this point, which means it would probably not even break into the top 1000 list of current infectious diseases spreading around the globe.</p>\n<p>So why the media hype and sudden attention by government health organizations like the WHO and the CDC?</p>\n<p>The first clue that this is a new &#8220;plandemic&#8221; is to see how Big Pharma is setup to profit from it, because disease management is first and foremost a marketing opportunity, and to create to the proper fear factor, one has to advertise a &#8220;new&#8221; and &#8220;deadly&#8221; disease to start the funds flowing through emergency use authorizations.</p>\n<p>And sure enough, that first criterion for identifying a &#8220;plandemic&#8221; has been met this week, as Whitney Webb reported:</p>\n<p>&#8220;In recent days, concern over a global outbreak of monkeypox&#8230;two companies are already cashing in. As concern over monkeypox has risen, so too have\xc2\xa0the shares\xc2\xa0of Emergent Biosolutions and SIGA Technologies. Both companies essentially have monopolies in the US market, and other markets as well, on smallpox vaccines and treatments. Their main smallpox-focused products are, conveniently, also used to protect against or treat monkeypox as well. As a result, the shares of Emergent Biosolutions climbed 12% on Thursday, while those of SIGA soared 17.1%.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The second sign to look for, is if this &#8220;new outbreak&#8221; has already been predicted beforehand, and even simulated in an effort to predict how to &#8220;contain the outbreak,&#8221; much as COVID-19 was weeks before the first alleged cases even showed up, with the pandemic simulation called Event 201.</p>\n<p>And thanks to some investigations by Polly St. George, there was indeed a simulation of a &#8220;monkeypox&#8221;
